<td style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Single-player_video_game" title="Single-player video game">Single-player</a>, <a href="/wiki/Multiplayer_video_game" title="Multiplayer video game">multiplayer</a></td>

<p><i><b>Battlefield 3</b></i> is a <a href="/wiki/First-person_shooter" title="First-person shooter">first-person shooter</a> <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video game</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/EA_DICE" title="EA DICE">EA DICE</a> and published by <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a>. It is a direct sequel to 2005's <i><a href="/wiki/Battlefield_2" title="Battlefield 2">Battlefield 2</a></i>, and the eleventh installment in the <i><a href="/wiki/Battlefield_(series)" title="Battlefield (series)">Battlefield</a></i> franchise.</p>
<p>The game was released in North America on 25 October 2011 and in Europe on 28 October 2011 for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BF3Online_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-BF3Online-4">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/EA_Mobile" title="EA Mobile">EA Mobile</a> also confirmed a port for the <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> platform. The game sold 5 million copies in its first week of release,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Copies_Sold_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Copies_Sold-5">[5]</a></sup> and received positive reviews from most game reviewers. It is the first game in the series that does not support versions of Windows prior to <a href="/wiki/Windows_Vista" title="Windows Vista">Windows Vista</a> as the game only supports <a href="/wiki/DirectX" title="DirectX">DirectX</a> 10 and 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-notXP_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-notXP-6">[6]</a></sup> The PC version is exclusive to EA's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Origin_(digital_distribution_platform)" title="Origin (digital distribution platform)">Origin</a> platform,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OriginRequired_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-OriginRequired-7">[7]</a></sup> through which PC users also authenticate when connecting to the game. The game's sequel, <i><a href="/wiki/Battlefield_4" title="Battlefield 4">Battlefield 4</a></i>, was released on 29 October 2013.</p>
<p>In <i>Battlefield 3</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s campaign, players take on the personas of several military roles: a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Marine" title="U.S. Marine">U.S. Marine</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Boeing_F/A-18E/F_Super_Hornet" title="Boeing F/A-18E/F Super Hornet">F-18</a> weapons system officer, an <a href="/wiki/M1_Abrams" title="M1 Abrams">M1A2 Abrams</a> tank operator, and a <a href="/wiki/Spetsnaz_GRU" title="Spetsnaz GRU">Spetsnaz GRU</a> operative. The campaign takes place in various locations, including <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>; and follows the stories of Sergeant Henry Blackburn and Dimitri Mayakovsky.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gameplay">Gameplay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Gameplay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battlefield_3_Paris.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="244" data-file-width="433" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/72/Battlefield_3_Paris.jpg/220px-Battlefield_3_Paris.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/72/Battlefield_3_Paris.jpg/330px-Battlefield_3_Paris.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/72/Battlefield_3_Paris.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battlefield_3_Paris.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Screenshot of the single-player campaign mode of <i>Battlefield 3</i>. Here, player character "<a href="#Setting_and_characters">Dima</a>" is armed with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G36C" title="G36C">G36C</a> carbine.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>Battlefield 3</i> features the <a href="/wiki/Combined_arms" title="Combined arms">combined arms</a> battles across single-player, co-operative and multiplayer modes. It reintroduces several elements absent from the <i><a href="/wiki/Battlefield:_Bad_Company" title="Battlefield: Bad Company">Bad Company</a></i> games, including fighter jets, the <a href="/wiki/Prone_position" title="Prone position">prone position</a> and 64-player battles on PC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gi-cover_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-gi-cover-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pcg-pc_lead_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-pcg-pc_lead-9">[9]</a></sup> To accommodate the lower player count on consoles, the ground area is limited for Xbox 360 and PS3, though fly space remains the same.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eurogamer_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-eurogamer-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>During an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Game_Informer" title="Game Informer">Game Informer</a></i>, EA stated that <a href="/wiki/Battlefield_2#Commander" title="Battlefield 2">Commander Mode</a> is unlikely to be included,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Battlefield_3_Blog_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Battlefield_3_Blog-11">[11]</a></sup> which was met with some criticism on the EA forum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The game features maps set in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a> (as well as other locations in <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>), <a href="/wiki/Sulaymaniyah" title="Sulaymaniyah">Sulaymaniyah</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a> and other parts of the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>. The maps cover urban streets, metropolitan downtown areas, and open landscapes suited to vehicle combat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cvg-ea_store_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-cvg-ea_store-13">[13]</a></sup> <i>Battlefield 3</i> introduces the "Battlelog"; a free cross-platform social service with built-in text messaging, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voice_over_Internet_Protocol" title="Voice over Internet Protocol">voice communications</a>, game statistics, and the ability to join games that friends are already playing (though both players need to be on the same platform).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooperative">Cooperative</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cooperative">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A demo featuring the new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Co-op_mode" title="Co-op mode">co-op mode</a> was featured at <a href="/wiki/Gamescom#Gamescom_2011" title="Gamescom">Gamescom 2011</a>. DICE general manager Karl Magnus Troedsson confirmed that a <a href="/wiki/Split_screen_(computer_graphics)" title="Split screen (computer graphics)">split screen</a> option will not be available in co-op mode.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> <i>Battlefield 3</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s new Battlelog social network, DICE noted, would be tied to all co-op matches, allowing players to try to beat friends' scores and to track their performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamescom_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-gamescom-16">[16]</a></sup> Participating in co-op mode allows the player to collect points that unlock additional content that can be used in multiplayer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Multiplayer">Multiplayer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Multiplayer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battlefield_3_Jet_HUD.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="325" data-file-width="640" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e3/Battlefield_3_Jet_HUD.jpg/220px-Battlefield_3_Jet_HUD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e3/Battlefield_3_Jet_HUD.jpg/330px-Battlefield_3_Jet_HUD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e3/Battlefield_3_Jet_HUD.jpg/440px-Battlefield_3_Jet_HUD.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battlefield_3_Jet_HUD.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Screenshot of the HUD as shown in the fighter jet in Multiplayer Mode.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>Battlefield 3</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s multiplayer matches see players take on one of four roles: Assault, Support, Engineer and Recon. The Assault class focuses on <a href="/wiki/Assault_rifle" title="Assault rifle">assault rifles</a> and healing teammates. The Support class focuses on <a href="/wiki/Light_machine_gun" title="Light machine gun">light machine guns</a> and supplying ammunition. The Engineer class focuses on supporting and destroying vehicles. The Recon class focuses on sniping and <a href="/wiki/Artillery_observer" title="Artillery observer">spotting</a> enemies. The mechanics of the weapons have been changed to utilize the new engine: compatible weapons may have <a href="/wiki/Bipod" title="Bipod">bipods</a> attached which can then be deployed when in the prone position or near suitable scenery, and provide a significant boost to accuracy and recoil reduction. Suppressive fire from weapons blurs the vision and reduces the accuracy of those under fire, as well as health regeneration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-battlefield_blog_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-battlefield_blog-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-battleblog_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-battleblog-19">[19]</a></sup> The Recon class can put a radio beacon anywhere on the map and all squad members will be able to spawn on the location of the beacon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several game modes are present, including Conquest, Rush, Squad Deathmatch, Squad Rush and for the first time since <i><a href="/wiki/Battlefield_1942" title="Battlefield 1942">Battlefield 1942</a></i>, Team Deathmatch. However, more game modes are available through the purchase of extra downloadable content packs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The PC version of <i>Battlefield 3</i> is by default launched via a web browser from the Battlelog web site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> A server browser is present in console versions of the game, however.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Synopsis">Synopsis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Synopsis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Setting_and_characters">Setting and characters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Setting and characters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Battlefield 3</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Campaign story is set during the fictional "War of 2014" and covers events that occur over the span of nine months. Most of the story takes place in the <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>–<a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> region. Other locations include the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijani</a> border; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paris,_France" title="Paris, France">Paris, France</a>; and <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, New York. Most missions occur as flashbacks on part of the interrogation of Staff Sergeant Henry Blackburn, and do not occur in order of events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Campaign puts the player in control of four different <a href="/wiki/Player_character" title="Player character">player characters</a>. For most of the story, the player controls <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Staff_Sergeant" title="Staff Sergeant">SSgt.</a> Henry "Black" Blackburn (portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Gideon_Emery" title="Gideon Emery">Gideon Emery</a>), a member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Marine_Corps" title="U.S. Marine Corps">U.S. Marine Corps</a> <a href="/wiki/1st_Reconnaissance_Battalion" title="1st Reconnaissance Battalion">1st Recon Battalion</a> and main <a href="/wiki/Protagonist" title="Protagonist">protagonist</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prima_ogg_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-prima_ogg-25">[25]</a></sup> The player also controls Sgt. Jonathan "Jono" Miller, a <a href="/wiki/M1_Abrams" title="M1 Abrams">M1 Abrams</a> tank operator deployed in Tehran;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thunderrun_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-thunderrun-26">[26]</a></sup> Lt. Jennifer "Wedge" Colby Hawkins, an <a href="/wiki/Boeing_F/A-18E/F_Super_Hornet" title="Boeing F/A-18E/F Super Hornet">F/A-18F Super Hornet</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weapon_Systems_Officer" title="Weapon Systems Officer">Weapon Systems Officer</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prima_ogg_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-prima_ogg-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-go_hunting_cine_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-go_hunting_cine-27">[27]</a></sup> and Dimitri "Dima" Mayakovsky, a Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GRU" title="GRU">GRU</a> operative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-comrades_cine_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-comrades_cine-28">[28]</a></sup> The main antagonist, Solomon, is an overseas asset for the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-24">[24]</a></sup> Non-player characters include: Misfit 1, Blackburn's squad (including David Montes, Steve Campo, Christian Matkovic, and Cpt. Quinton Cole); Dima's GRU squadmates Vladimir and Kiril; and CIA Agents Gordon and Whistler, who interrogate Blackburn for much of the Campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 15 March, Sgt. Blackburn's squad, Misfit 1-3, attempted to find and safely return a US squad investigating an <a href="/wiki/Improvised_explosive_device" title="Improvised explosive device">improvised explosive device</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sulaymaniyah" title="Sulaymaniyah">Sulaymaniyah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Kurdistan" title="Iraqi Kurdistan">Iraqi Kurdistan</a>, whose last known position was in territory controlled by the PLR (People's Liberation &amp; Resistance), an Iranian paramilitary insurgent group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-op_swordbreaker_cine_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-op_swordbreaker_cine-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tru_achieve_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-tru_achieve-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> They find the missing squad, which had been ambushed by the PLR; but before they can escape the city, a massive earthquake wrecks the city. Blackburn, fellow squadmate Montes, and other survivors fight their way out of the ruins of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uprising_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-uprising-32">[32]</a></sup> On the same day, the PLR stage a <i><a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, turning it into a <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">military dictatorship</a>, and the US subsequently invades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-go_hunting_cine_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-go_hunting_cine-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uprising_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-uprising-32">[32]</a></sup> Lt. Hawkins takes part in a raid on enemy fighters over Iran and an air strike over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mehrabad_Airport" title="Mehrabad Airport">Mehrabad Airport</a>. In the aftermath of the air strikes, Misfit 1 was sent into <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a> to perform battle damage assessment and apprehend the leader of the PLR, Faruk Al-Bashir.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-go_hunting_cine_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-go_hunting_cine-27">[27]</a></sup> While investigating an underground bank vault in the target's suspected location, Blackburn and his team learn that the PLR have acquired Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suitcase_nuke" title="Suitcase nuke">suitcase nukes</a>, with two of the three devices missing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Being overrun, Misfit requests backup from an <a href="/wiki/M1_Abrams" title="M1 Abrams">M1 Abrams</a> column "Anvil 3", including Sergeant Miller. Miller facilitates Misfit 1's helicopter extraction, but is captured when waiting for the arrival of the Quick Reaction Force. Miller is promptly executed by Solomon and Al-Bashir, with the event being filmed and posted on the Internet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Battlefield_3_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Battlefield_3-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Later, Misfit 1-3 manages to capture Al-Bashir, who becomes fatally wounded when they cause his escape vehicle to crash. Realizing that he had been betrayed and used, Al-Bashir reveals some of Solomon's plan—to detonate the nukes in Paris and New York City—before succumbing to his wounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Misfit 1 gets a lead on arms dealer Amir Kaffarov, who was working with Solomon and Al-Bashir.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> They attempt to capture Kaffarov from his villa on the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> coast, near the Azerbaijani border. However, they run into a <a href="/wiki/Russian_Airborne_Troops" title="Russian Airborne Troops">Russian paratrooper</a> battalion, also after Kaffarov, who engage them with airdropped <a href="/wiki/BMP-2" title="BMP-2">BMP-2s</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-25" title="Sukhoi Su-25">Su-25s</a> providing <a href="/wiki/Close_air_support" title="Close air support">close air support</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> In the ensuing chaos, Blackburn's squadmates, Campo and Matkovic, are killed in an enemy airstrike.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Battlefield_3_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-Battlefield_3-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Meanwhile, a <a href="/wiki/Spetsnaz" title="Spetsnaz">Spetsnaz</a> team led by Dima assaults Kaffarov's villa. Kaffarov tries to bribe his way out, but Dima beats him up nonetheless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Battlefield_3_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-Battlefield_3-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Blackburn arrives at the villa and finds Dima and a presumed dead Kaffarov. Dima reveals Solomon's plot to Blackburn, and requests his cooperation to prevent "a war between [their] nations". Meanwhile, Misfit 1's commanding officer Cole arrives, and Blackburn is forced to shoot his superior before he can kill Dima.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Blackburn's shooting of his commanding officer results in his eight-hour interrogation by the C.I.A. at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunters_Point,_Queens" title="Hunters Point, Queens">Hunters Point, Queens</a>.</p>
<p>During Blackburn's captivity, Dima's Spetsnaz squad attempts to stop the attack in Paris. However, Vladimir is impaled and dies, and the nuke explodes, killing 80,000 people. Meanwhile, the CIA agents do not believe Blackburn's story, since Solomon is a CIA informant, and there is no concrete proof of his involvement in the terrorist attacks. They instead believe that Russia is responsible for the attacks, and that Dima has tricked Blackburn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>With no other options, Blackburn and surviving squad member Montes break out of captivity to stop the attack in New York. Evading police, Blackburn manages to break into a hijacked subway train, full of Solomon's men and explosive charges. He works his way to the front car, where he is ambushed by Solomon. When ambushed by Solomon, Blackburn gains the upper hand by obtaining and activating the detonator, causing the train to crash. Blackburn pursues Solomon through the sewers and up to street level. Montes, having obtained a police car, picks up Blackburn and engages Solomon and the PLR in a brief vehicular chase, which ends with both cars crashing in <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a>. As a bewildered crowd watches on, Solomon shoots Montes, but Blackburn manages to kill Solomon by bludgeoning him to death with a brick in the ensuing brawl and recovers the nuclear bomb.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the epilogue, it is revealed that Dima had survived the Paris detonation, albeit suffering <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radiation_poisoning" title="Radiation poisoning">radiation poisoning</a> from the blast. He writes about the efforts of both himself and Blackburn to stop Solomon's plan "to set fire to the world". As he finishes, he examines a pistol, and seems to point it towards his head. A knock comes from his door, the screen cuts to black, and the last sound is that of the pistol being loaded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Battlefield 3</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s lead platform was originally the <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">PC</a> until it was switched to <a href="/wiki/Video_game_console" title="Video game console">consoles</a> midway through development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a> version of <i>Battlefield 3</i> is shipped on two discs due to the disc size limit;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> however, the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PS3</a> version ships on one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a>.</p>
<p><i>Battlefield 3</i> debuts the new <a href="/wiki/Frostbite_(game_engine)" title="Frostbite (game engine)">Frostbite 2</a> engine. This updated Frostbite engine can realistically portray the destruction of buildings and scenery to a greater extent than previous versions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pbf2_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-pbf2-47">[47]</a></sup> Unlike previous iterations, the new version can also support dense urban areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frostbite2_e3_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-frostbite2_e3-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Battlefield 3</i> uses a new type of character animation technology called ANT. ANT technology is used in <a href="/wiki/EA_Sports" title="EA Sports">EA Sports</a> games, such as <i><a href="/wiki/FIFA_(video_game_series)" title="FIFA (video game series)">FIFA</a></i>, but for <i>Battlefield 3</i> is adapted to create a more realistic soldier, with the ability to transition into cover and turn the head before the body, as well as "drag fallen comrades into safety and mount weapons on almost any part of the terrain".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cvg-ea_store_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-cvg-ea_store-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pbf_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-pbf-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="PlayStation_3_exclusive_content">PlayStation 3 exclusive content</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: PlayStation 3 exclusive content">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 6 June 2011, during <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E3_2011" title="E3 2011">E3 2011</a> press conference, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Tretton" title="Jack Tretton">Jack Tretton</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Computer_Entertainment_of_America" title="Sony Computer Entertainment of America">Sony Computer Entertainment of America</a> announced that the PlayStation 3 version of the game would be bundled with a free copy of <i><a href="/wiki/Battlefield_1943" title="Battlefield 1943">Battlefield 1943</a></i>, however, at launch, the game wasn't included.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> EA then said that <i>Battlefield 3</i> PlayStation 3 owners would receive timed-exclusive DLC for the game instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> On 20 November 2011, Law firm Edelson McGuire took EA to court on behalf of disappointed gamers. The complaint focuses on EA's communication of the change of plan, second proposal with early DLC that had already been announced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Shortly after EA was threatened with being taken to court over its failure to deliver the free game as announced at E3, EA announced they will offer owners of the PlayStation 3 version of <i>Battlefield 3</i> a free downloadable copy of <i>Battlefield 1943</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wii_U_version">Wii U version</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Wii U version">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 7 June 2011, during <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E3_2011" title="E3 2011">E3 2011</a> press conference, <a href="/wiki/John_Riccitiello" title="John Riccitiello">John Riccitiello</a> of EA games expressed interest in Nintendo's upcoming system, the <a href="/wiki/Wii_U" title="Wii U">Wii U</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Patrick Liu, the executive producer of <i>Battlefield 3</i>, stated that <a href="/wiki/EA_DICE" title="EA DICE">EA DICE</a> currently have no games in development for the Wii U and a port for the console "probably won't happen".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beta">Beta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Beta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The open beta commenced on 29 September 2011, for all platforms,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> and ended on 10 October 2011. 48 hour early access was granted to players who bought the Tier 1 edition of <i><a href="/wiki/Medal_of_Honor_(2010_video_game)" title="Medal of Honor (2010 video game)">Medal of Honor</a></i> or pre-ordered the digital version of <i>Battlefield 3: Limited Edition</i> through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Origin_(digital_distribution_platform)" title="Origin (digital distribution platform)">Origin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bfblog_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-bfblog-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Soundtrack">Soundtrack</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Soundtrack">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="infobox vevent haudio" style="width:22em">
<tr>
<th class="summary album" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-style: italic; background-color: gainsboro">Battlefield 3 (Original Video Game Soundtrack)</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th class="description" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: gainsboro"><a href="/wiki/Soundtrack_album" title="Soundtrack album">Soundtrack album</a> by <span class="contributor">Johan Skugge &amp; Jukka Rintamäki</span></th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Released</th>
<td class="published">24 October 2011<span style="display:none"> (<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2011-10-24</span>)</span> <small>(digital)</small></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Music_genre" title="Music genre">Genre</a></th>
<td class="category"><a href="/wiki/Video_game_music" title="Video game music">Video game soundtrack</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Length</th>
<td>35:59</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A soundtrack album was released on 24 October 2011, one day before the game was released. It is available on iTunes and Amazon. The music was composed by Johan Skugge and Jukka Rintamäki.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Easter_eggs">Easter eggs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Easter eggs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Battlefield 3</i> and its five DLC packs contain numerous <a href="/wiki/Easter_egg_(media)" title="Easter egg (media)">Easter eggs</a>. Hiding in obscure areas of the game are references to other Electronic Arts games and franchises including <i><a href="/wiki/Mirror%27s_Edge" title="Mirror's Edge">Mirror's Edge</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Mass_Effect" title="Mass Effect">Mass Effect</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Some sources suggested other Easter eggs pointed to future <i>Battlefield</i> games or DLC packs. During the firefight in the mall trying to protect Al-Bashir, the store in which they are defending Al-Bashir has copy's of games on the shelf and one game being titled "Frostbite" which references the engine used by Battlefield 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> A wall on the multiplayer map "Wake Island" featuring the number 2143 and a futuristic hovercraft on a different map in the <i>End Game</i> DLC have been said to suggest a follow up to 2006's <i><a href="/wiki/Battlefield_2142" title="Battlefield 2142">Battlefield 2142</a></i> is in the works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Several <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">dinosaur</a> Easter eggs—such as a flying <a href="/wiki/Pterodactylus" title="Pterodactylus">pterodactyl</a> on the map "Nebandan Flats" and <a href="/wiki/Tyrannosaurus" title="Tyrannosaurus">tyrannosaurus</a> skulls or toy statues on various maps—have led others to believe a dinosaur-related game or DLC would be released in the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The idea of a dinosaur-related minigame originated from fan feedback through social media outlets prior to <i>Battlefield 3</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Neither of these possible upcoming games has been confirmed by EA.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing_and_release">Marketing and release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Marketing and release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Battlefield 3</i> was revealed on 3 February 2011, by video game magazine <i>Game Informer</i>. The coverage included information on building the game and interviews with DICE, as well as three trailers: a teaser and the first two parts in a series of gameplay from the level "Fault Line".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Several other trailers were released showing different aspects of the game, including both single and multiplayer, as well as emphasizing the new engine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bf3_videos_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-bf3_videos-70">[70]</a></sup> On 16 August 2011, co-op gameplay and a "Caspian Border Multiplayer Gameplay Trailer" were shown at <a href="/wiki/Gamescom#Gamescom_2011" title="Gamescom">Gamescom 2011</a> illustrating the co-op mode and the first footage of air combat, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamescom_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-gamescom-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Trailer releases gained momentum in the week before the release of the game. EA released a multiplayer trailer which showed the variety of maps available in multiplayer, with short scenes of actual gameplay. It also featured shots of a map that is included in the "Back to Karkand" <a href="/wiki/Downloadable_content" title="Downloadable content">downloadable content</a> (DLC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> EA released a launch trailer, showing off the various missions in the single-player campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>EA CEO John Riccitiello stated that <i>Battlefield 3</i> is aimed at competing with the <i><a href="/wiki/Call_of_Duty" title="Call of Duty">Call of Duty</a></i> series. EA planned on spending over $100 million on a marketing campaign for <i>Battlefield 3</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Electronic Arts stated that <i>Battlefield 3</i> is a "flat out superior" to <i>Call of Duty</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> EA has said it is going on the "offense" in regards to its marketing on <i>Battlefield 3</i>, saying that it started its campaign early to establish a "beachhead".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Anyone who had watched a trailer for the upcoming film <i><a href="/wiki/Act_of_Valor" title="Act of Valor">Act of Valor</a></i> through the official <i>Battlefield 3</i> website could receive free downloadable dogtags for use with any version of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 2017, the game was made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Backwards_compatible" title="Backwards compatible">backwards compatible</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a> (alongside <i><a href="/wiki/Battlefield:_Bad_Company_2" title="Battlefield: Bad Company 2">Battlefield: Bad Company 2</a></i>) and was subsequently added to the <a href="/wiki/EA_Access" title="EA Access">EA Access</a> service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-order_promotion">Pre-order promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Pre-order promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>All pre-orders of the <i>Limited Edition</i> grant free access to the "Back to Karkand" DLC pack, a reference to the "Strike at Karkand" map (a popular <i>Battlefield 2</i> map), to include four maps brought over from <i>Battlefield 2</i>, 10 new weapons, 4 new vehicles, 5 new achievements/trophies, and a new addition to the series, "Assignments". The maps from the expansion pack will be: Strike at Karkand, Gulf of Oman, Wake Island, and Sharqi Peninsula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Back_to_Karkand_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Back_to_Karkand-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pre-ordering at selected retailers and Origin included the "Physical Warfare Pack", granting access to time-based exclusive weapons and items; including a light machine gun, a sniper rifle accessory, and armor-piercing ammunition. Also included is launch day access to the DAO-12 semi-automatic shotgun, which other players can unlock through game play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pack-reveal_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-pack-reveal-80">[80]</a></sup> Pre-order at select retailers also provide the "SPECACT Kit Upgrade", the "Dog Tag Pack" and <i>Battlefield 3</i> gear for the player's console avatar. Pre-ordering at Origin gave players a shotgun and beret for <i><a href="/wiki/Battlefield_Play4Free" title="Battlefield Play4Free">Battlefield Play4Free</a></i>, and 48 hour early access to the <i>Battlefield 3</i> beta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bfblog_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-bfblog-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Originally the "Physical Warfare Pack" was to be exclusive to pre-orders, but fan reaction to this was negative, causing EA to clarify that it would be made available to all players for free later in the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ars-physwarpack_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-ars-physwarpack-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ars-eaphyswarpackresp_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-ars-eaphyswarpackresp-82">[82]</a></sup> On 2 September 2011, a trailer for the Physical Warfare Pack was released on YouTube showing all the content included within the pack in action in-game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>All the content except the "Back to Karkand" pack was available from day one. The pack was released on 6 December 2011 for the PlayStation 3, and a week later for the Xbox 360 and PC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2Krelease_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-B2Krelease-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_pass">Online pass</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Online pass">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>To access the game's online multiplayer mode on consoles, players need to activate an <a href="/wiki/Online_pass" title="Online pass">online pass</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vgpass_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-vgpass-85">[85]</a></sup> New copies of the game include one online pass for the original owner of the game to access the multiplayer; however, if a player buys a used copy or rents the game, they must purchase an online pass separately, or access a 48-hour trial via the official game site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vgpass_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-vgpass-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> When asked why the developers implemented the pass system, game designer Alan Kertz replied, "because servers cost money, and used games don't make developers any money."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vgpass_85-2"><a href="#cite_note-vgpass-85">[85]</a></sup> Some of the online pass codes were invalid from the time of purchase, which EA responded to by telling affected consumers to ask the retailer for a replacement code.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EA_Help_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-EA_Help-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Downloadable_content">Downloadable content</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Downloadable content">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Back_to_Karkand"><i>Back to Karkand</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Back to Karkand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first pack of <a href="/wiki/Downloadable_content" title="Downloadable content">downloadable content</a> (DLC), "Back to Karkand", was announced before launch and was released on 13 December 2011 for PC and Xbox 360, while PlayStation 3 owners received it a week earlier. It was priced at $15 USD but was free for all users who purchased the limited edition. It features four maps remade from <i>Battlefield 2</i>, three new vehicles and ten new weapons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Close_Quarters"><i>Close Quarters</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Close Quarters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At GDC 2012 DICE revealed it would release three more DLCs. The second DLC, "Close Quarters" arrived in June 2012 featuring four new infantry-oriented maps, ten new weapons, HD Destruction, ten new assignments, five unique Dogtags, and a new game mode, Conquest Domination, a Conquest mode adapted for smaller spaces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armored_Kill"><i>Armored Kill</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Armored Kill">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The third DLC, "Armored Kill" arrived on 4 September 2012 for premium PlayStation 3 users and 11 September for Xbox 360 and PC users. The DLC was made available for non-premium PlayStation 3 and Xbox 360 users on 25 September 2012. Armored Kill included new vehicles, specifically tanks, ATVs, and mobile artillery, as well as new vehicle-oriented maps and what is called "the biggest map in Battlefield history".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath"><i>Aftermath</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A DLC titled "Aftermath" was revealed in a trailer for <i>Battlefield 3</i> Premium. It was released to PlayStation 3 Premium subscribers on 27 November 2012 and to PC and Xbox 360 Premium subscribers on 4 December 2012. "Aftermath" was released to non-Premium subscribers on PlayStation 3 on 11 December 2012, and on PC and Xbox 360 on 18 December 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> A video released by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EA_Digital_Illusions_CE" title="EA Digital Illusions CE">DICE games</a> revealed that there would be a crossbow, with customizable scopes and various <a href="/wiki/Crossbow_bolt" title="Crossbow bolt">bolts</a> before its release.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="End_Game"><i>End Game</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: End Game">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The fifth DLC, "End Game", was released for PlayStation 3 Premium members on 5 March 2013 and to PC and Xbox 360 Premium members on 12 March 2013, then to non-Premium PlayStation 3 players on 19 March 2013 and to PC and Xbox 360 players on 26 March 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Novel">Novel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Novel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Andy_McNab" title="Andy McNab">Andy McNab</a> penned a tie-in novel called <i><b>Battlefield 3: The Russian</b></i>, which follows the story of GRU Spetsnaz commando <a href="#Setting_and_characters">Dmitri "Dima" Mayakovsky</a> and his involvement against the PLR, as well as his connection to the antagonist, <a href="#Setting_and_characters">Solomon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bf3_tr_prologue_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-bf3_tr_prologue-94">[94]</a></sup> McNab also served as the game's consultant on military tactics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The novel was released on 25 October 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<tr>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Official_Xbox_Magazine" title="Official Xbox Magazine"><i>OXM</i> (US)</a></td>
<td style="text-align:center;font-size:110%">9/10<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BF3-OXM_Review_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-BF3-OXM_Review-115">[115]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i>Battlefield 3</i> has received mostly positive reviews. <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> gave it a score of 9.0 out of 10.0 for all platforms,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> and praised the graphics and multiplayer game. Even though it criticized the single-player campaign story, and the occasional glitches of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frostbite_2" title="Frostbite 2">game engine</a>, it still gave the game a mostly positive review, "Regardless of the narrative missteps or the occasional glitches, Battlefield 3 offers an unforgettable, world-class multiplayer suite that's sure to excite shooter fans."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ignreview_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-ignreview-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Joystiq" title="Joystiq">Joystiq</a> awarded the game 4.5 out of 5 stars, stating that the campaign was "tactically linear" and that the A.I. within the game were "murderously un-fun to fight". Complaints were also made of the multiplayer aspect, stating that destruction was less than expected: "It's not <i><a href="/wiki/Battlefield:_Bad_Company_2" title="Battlefield: Bad Company 2">Bad Company 2</a></i>, and levels won't start out intact and end looking like the surface of the moon the way they often did in that game." They did, however, praise the multiplayer experience as "unmatched", stating that this should be the sole reason to buy the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jsreview_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-jsreview-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/GameSpot" title="GameSpot">GameSpot</a> gave <i>Battlefield 3</i> a score of 8.5 out of 10 across all platforms. They praised the deep multiplayer mode, great variety of vehicles, many well-designed environments, and a great reward system for team play; however, they criticized the campaign for being "dull and disappointing" and using a "familiar formula". The cooperative mode was viewed favorably; the only criticism on the cooperative missions was that "there aren't more of them to keep you busy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GSpot_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-GSpot-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Official_Xbox_Magazine" title="Official Xbox Magazine">Official Xbox Magazine</a></i> gave the game 9 out of 10, commending the game for its multiplayer mode, but criticizing the solo campaign. Similarly, <i>Official Xbox Magazine</i> (UK) gave the game 8 out of 10, applauding its multiplayer gaming and calling it "The most expansive, refined Battlefield multiplayer yet" while also criticizing the single-player experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales_and_revenue">Sales and revenue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sales and revenue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to EA, <i>Battlefield 3</i> garnered 3 million pre-orders by the day of its release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> The pre-order total makes it "the biggest first-person shooter launch in EA history", according to the publisher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Two days after launch, EA CEO John Riccitiello announced via a conference call to investors that <i>Battlefield 3</i> has already shipped 10 million units within a week of release, with 3 million of those being pre-orders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a> stated that the title sold 5 million units within the first week of availability, easily becoming its fastest-selling game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> After one month, EA chief financial officer Eric Brown announced <i>Battlefield 3</i> had sold 8 million copies, and that the publisher has shipped 12 million copies of the game to retailers, 2 million more than it shipped for launch week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Peter Moore, the high-profile COO of EA, insisted that <i>Battlefield 3</i> successfully captured a slice of <i><a href="/wiki/Call_of_Duty:_Modern_Warfare_3" title="Call of Duty: Modern Warfare 3">Call of Duty: Modern Warfare 3</a></i>’s market share.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> On 29 June 2012 EA revealed that the game has sold 15 million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Japan, <i>Battlefield 3</i> had sold around 123,379 copies for the PlayStation 3 and 27,723 copies for the Xbox 360 when it was released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> In the first week, the game had sold 18,792 copies for the PlayStation 3 for a total of 142,171 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> The PlayStation 3 version later sold 8,094 copies for a total of 150,265 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_responses">Other responses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Battlefield_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Other responses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A scene in which the player is prompted to kill a rat that is attacking their character was criticized by <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals</a> (PETA). In a press release issued by the organization's German office, it claimed that the game "treats animals in a sadistic manner". The release also went further on to say that the scene can have "a brutalising effect on the young male target audience".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>The reproduction of various scenes in <i>Battlefield 3</i> are highly accurate of their real-life counterparts such as the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bazaar,_Tehran" title="Grand Bazaar, Tehran">Grand Bazaar</a>. Iran has reacted to the scenes set within Iran by banning the sale of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> As the game had not been officially released in the country, the authorities were strictly enforcing the prevention of the distribution of pirated copies of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> This comes after Iranian gamers had protested the release of the game and called for an apology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EA_Digital_Illusions_CE" title="EA Digital Illusions CE">EA Digital Illusions CE</a> (25 October – 2 November 2011). <i>Battlefield 3</i>. <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>/<a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a>/<a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>/<a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>. <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sega" title="Sega">Sega</a>. Solomon's using the PLR. He has at least two targets: New York and Paris. He's using public transit to move the weapons. He's going to detonate the New York device in Times Square very soon. <i>[shakes head]</i> …This cannot happen. We can avert war between our nations. Just two of us. No politicians, no money changing hands. Just two soldiers speaking the truth. Help me. Help me to do this. <i>[Blackburn hears someone kick a door open close by.]</i> That's it, I have to leave now. You don't shoot him, millions will die. / <b>Cole</b>: <i>[coming in, aiming at Dima]</i> Get down on the ground!</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABattlefield+3&amp;rft.au=EA+Digital+Illusions+CE&amp;rft.btitle=Battlefield+3&amp;rft.date=2011-10-25%2F2011-11-02&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.pages=Level%2Farea%3A+Kaffarov&amp;rft.pub=Electronic+Arts%2C+Sega&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
